    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer17123593312180706771">Philip Latinowics is a successful but disillusioned painter who returns to his hometown on Croatia's Danubian plain after an absence of twenty-three years. He hopes that revisiting his cultural roots will inspire him to create the perfect work of art and thereby restore his faith in both art and life. Haunted by his troubled childhood, however, he falls in with shady chara</span>
  <span id="freeText17123593312180706771" style="display:none">Philip Latinowics is a successful but disillusioned painter who returns to his hometown on Croatia's Danubian plain after an absence of twenty-three years. He hopes that revisiting his cultural roots will inspire him to create the perfect work of art and thereby restore his faith in both art and life. Haunted by his troubled childhood, however, he falls in with shady characters and discovers the emotional, intellectual, and imaginative poverty of his background.</span>

    <a title="Jovan Autonoma≈°eviƒá" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69438797-jovan-autonoma-evi"><img alt="Jovan Autonoma≈°eviƒá" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500034872p2/69438797.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2096582859?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jovan Autonoma≈°eviƒá" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jovan Autonoma≈°eviƒá" href="/user/show/69438797-jovan-autonoma-evi">Jovan Autonoma≈°eviƒá</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9531505705" href="/book/show/2541127.Povratak_Filipa_Latinovicza">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096582859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8356673219725238161">A curious but classic book, which I've read twice. An artist returns home after 20 years abroad, to face up to the personal demons that send him into exile in the first place. It's a trip into the stifling and stuffy world of provincial Habsburg aristocracy, their endless intrigues, backbiting, and attempts to move up the foodchain and avoid the fate worse than death - having to work for a living. How such a society is ultimately doomed to self-destruction, and how hard it is for anyone born int</span>
  <span id="freeText8356673219725238161" style="display:none">A curious but classic book, which I've read twice. An artist returns home after 20 years abroad, to face up to the personal demons that send him into exile in the first place. It's a trip into the stifling and stuffy world of provincial Habsburg aristocracy, their endless intrigues, backbiting, and attempts to move up the foodchain and avoid the fate worse than death - having to work for a living. How such a society is ultimately doomed to self-destruction, and how hard it is for anyone born into it to live a normal life without emigrating. We see this world through the artist's eye, as despite himself he is constantly inspired by the coarse world around him to create new paintings, that capture the rawness of country life and elevate it to the eternal. Interesting parallels with today's HDZ, the dominant political party in Croatia since the war, and a haven for the unscrupulously ambitious. Croatia is also undergoing a demographic crisis as young people leave in droves for the more established EU countries (as they are from the rest of the Balkans). Go west! Very well written, long and complex sentences ensnare and suffocate the reader in the moribund world described by the author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8356673219725238161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15044182060231105629">When I heard this was considered one of the major works of Croatian literature I realised with a guilty start I had never read ANY Croatian literature. Now I have read this, my life feels a little less incomplete. So for that reason alone I‚Äôm glad I read it, but the experience was somewhat mixed.<br/><br/>I have to say that unlike a lot of novels this one gets better and better towards the end, and becomes very dramatic, with several alarming revelations and an ending of horrifying high drama. I also like</span>
  <span id="freeText15044182060231105629" style="display:none">When I heard this was considered one of the major works of Croatian literature I realised with a guilty start I had never read ANY Croatian literature. Now I have read this, my life feels a little less incomplete. So for that reason alone I‚Äôm glad I read it, but the experience was somewhat mixed.<br /><br />I have to say that unlike a lot of novels this one gets better and better towards the end, and becomes very dramatic, with several alarming revelations and an ending of horrifying high drama. I also liked the vivid descriptions, and the thought provoking treatment of art. Philip‚Äôs mother is upset at his portrait of her. So should art always strive to tell the truth? One feels many relationships would break down into anguished chaos if we always did.<br /><br />Philip mocks the limited intellectual horizons and artistic tastes of everyone else. The main effect of this is not to make them look stupid but to make him look arrogant and unpleasant. At one point he also strikes a woman ‚Äì anyone who does this, in the pages of a novel or in real life, instantly forfeits my sympathy. The character of Dr Kyriales is confusing ‚Äì is he a madman, a criminal, a liar? Perhaps all three? The discussions of metaphysics with him are extremely tedious and the dullest part of the book. <br /><br />So although there was much to enjoy here there was also quite a bit to dislike, and I also felt a little out of sympathy with Philip‚Äôs aesthetic sensibilities. He has a huge disdain for Habsburg baroque, whereas in an ideal world I would live surrounded by it. One can never have enough ormolu clocks and stucco cherubs, I find. And what was so great about the aesthetic that replaced it ‚Äì the drear gritty proletarianism of Yugoslav communism? Grey concrete, terrible clothes, and tower blocks? No thanks‚Ä¶.<br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10529830723649955355">HR; <br/>Povratak Filipa Latinovivza je klasiƒçno djelo hrvatske knji≈æevnosti jednog od najpoznatijih autora, uvr≈°teno u obveznu srednjo≈°kolsku lektiru i dr≈æavnu maturu.<br/>Iako te≈æe za shvatiti, ne bi trebalo predstavljati problem tipiƒçnom ƒçitaƒçu niti srednjo≈°kolcu.<br/><br/>Djelo (ƒçija je radnja u Hrvata opƒáa kultura) za tematiku uzima ≈æivot i dilemu jednog mu≈°kog lika koji predstavlja svoj ≈æivot i odnos s majkom koja se predstavlja kao udovica njegova oca, iako je okolina ilitiga "kom≈°iluk" vidi kao lokalnu kurt</span>
  <span id="freeText10529830723649955355" style="display:none">HR; <br />Povratak Filipa Latinovivza je klasiƒçno djelo hrvatske knji≈æevnosti jednog od najpoznatijih autora, uvr≈°teno u obveznu srednjo≈°kolsku lektiru i dr≈æavnu maturu.<br />Iako te≈æe za shvatiti, ne bi trebalo predstavljati problem tipiƒçnom ƒçitaƒçu niti srednjo≈°kolcu.<br /><br />Djelo (ƒçija je radnja u Hrvata opƒáa kultura) za tematiku uzima ≈æivot i dilemu jednog mu≈°kog lika koji predstavlja svoj ≈æivot i odnos s majkom koja se predstavlja kao udovica njegova oca, iako je okolina ilitiga "kom≈°iluk" vidi kao lokalnu kurtizanu. Filip svog oca nije nikada upoznao, no pri zavr≈°etku djela mo≈æemo i sami vidjeti da on shvaƒáa tko je taj ƒçovjek bio.<br /><br />Filip u odreƒëenoj dobi bje≈æi od kuƒáe i probija se kroz ≈æivot, te se vraƒáa kako bi vidio svoju majku; koja tvrdi da ga ne pozna i tjera ga sa svoga praga, pri ƒçemu mo≈æemo i sami osjetiti i do≈æivjeti njegove osjeƒáaje.<br /><br />Ovo je djelo doista klasik hrvatske pa ƒçak i balkanske knji≈æevnosti te bi ga svatko iole kulturan trebao proƒçitati i poznavati.<br /><br /><br />ENG; <br />The Return of Filip Latinovicz is a classic of croatian literature one of the most famous croatian authors, included in the mandatory high school reading list and state graduation program. Though harder to understand, it should not present a problem to a typical reader or a highschool student.<br /><br />This piece of literature (whose contet is common knowledge for the Croats) takes a subject of a male character that shows us his life, his dilemmas and his relationship with his mother, who presents herself as his fathers widow, though the neighbourhood sees her as a local courtesan. <br />Filip never met his father, but by the end of the story we can see that he understands who the man really was.<br /><br />At a certain age he runs away from home, fights his way through life and returnes home to see his mother; she refuses to open the door to a "stranger" and chases him away from her doorstep, and we can feel and live his emotions.<br /><br />This piece of literature is truly a classic of croatian, even balkanian literature and anyone even a little bit cultured should read and know.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RAGjSE6bQ9mtMHYWStrLssgJitIhSbKHffgVZ9OHG6eusXld6gWeCGFw9KHoT4kHLuqFSFvZd/wcNvpVnyDL/Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_11553583'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11553583-prokleta-avlija?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Prokleta avlija<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/2147.Ivo_Andri_?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Ivo Andriƒá<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.30 avg rating &mdash; 7,169 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1954\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer14058263970491405916\">Prokleta avlija/The Damned Yard (Description from Ivo Andriƒá Foundation website)\n\nThe novel is written in 1954. ƒÜamil, a wealthy young man of Smyrna living in the last years of the Ottoman Empire, is fascinated by the story of D≈æem, ill-fated brother<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText14058263970491405916\" style=\"display:none\">Prokleta avlija/The Damned Yard (Description from Ivo Andriƒá Foundation website)\n\nThe novel is written in 1954. ƒÜamil, a wealthy young man of Smyrna living in the last years of the Ottoman Empire, is fascinated by the story of D≈æem, ill-fated brother of the Sultan Bajazet, who ruled Turkey in the fifteenth century. ƒÜamil, in his isolation, comes to believe that he is D≈æem, and that he shares his evil destiny: he is born to be a victim of the State. Because of his stories about D≈æem‚Äôs ambitions to overthrow his brother, ƒÜamil is arrested under suspicion of plotting against the Sultan. He is taken to a prison in Istanbul, where he tells his story, to Petar, a monk.\n\nOut of these exotic materials, Andriƒá has constructed a book of great clarity, brevity and interest. No doubt it will be read by some as a political parable about the tyranny of the State, but also as a quite simply story about ill-fortune and human misunderstanding, fear and ignorance. D≈æem and ƒÜamil are doomed ‚Äì and the certainty of their persecution is sometimes relieved, sometimes intensified by the stupidity and fright of the people who cross their ill-starred lives.\n\nConstruction takes up most of the book‚Äôs space: the central story of D≈æem as related by ƒÜamil lasts only a chapter or two. For the rest of the time the reader strips layer off layer, as one narrator passes him on the next. There is an interesting passage that helps to explain this method, at the moment when ƒÜamil starts narrating D≈æem‚Äôs story in the first person. ‚ÄúI‚Äù is a word, we are told, which fixes the position of the speaker in such a way that the exercise of will is no longer possible, and the speaker strength is exceeded ‚Äì strength, presumably, to break out of the identification that all his past actions and thoughts force upon him when he uses the word. ‚ÄúI‚Äù is both a confession and an imprisonment. The fact that the novel passes the reader on from one narrator to the next rather suggests that the author is taking constant evasive action, lest he betray himself or his reader into the kind of ‚Äúpersonal confession‚Äù which seals the fate of ƒÜamil. What exactly this game of form flirting with meaning signifies, must be left to the individual reader.\n\nThe movement is centripetal, towards D≈æem‚Äôs story, and then disperses. Details within the story are made to mimic this form. Thus when Peter receives the message telling him of his impending release:\n\n‚ÄúTwo younger prisoners...were chasing around using him as the centerpoint of ever narrowing circles. Annoyed, he tried to break away from these exuberant youths when one of them brushed against him and he felt a folded scrap of paper thrust into his hand. The youths continued their chase but now in widening circles...‚Äù\n\nThe reader is led on just such a chase in the course of the novel. The effect of this is to make the plot seem more like a poetic image than an ordinary plot: capable, therefore, of as many meanings as are the images of an allusive poem. Yet the language is simple and direct, not at all ‚Äúpoetic‚Äù. The characters are remarkable alive, even in conversation. Karaƒëoz, the governor of the goal, is a spidery authoritarian, who loves to torment the charges he loves. The prisoners ‚Äúcomplained about the way one complains about one‚Äôs life and curses one‚Äôs destiny...it would have been hard for them to imagine life without him‚Äù.\n\n‚ÄúThe Devil‚Äôs Yard‚Äù is justified, as all symbolic and figurative novels must be, by the extent to which it touches the emotions. It is extremely moving. Fear, horror, despair, amusement at times ‚Äì all these indicate that the threat of the meaning has been recognized.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"14058263970491405916\" href=\"#\"         $('bookCover_8981458').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_8981458').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_8981458').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
